--- 帖子 #1 ---
I've been trading this system with some success, the Monday-Tuesday system (MoTu). My first post, time to give back to the community!
Pairs: I prefer GBP crosses. Probably any volatile pair.
Logic behind the system: The highs and lows of Monday and Tuesday often form the low or the high of the week.

Steps (see attached calculator)Find the highest high and lowest low of Monday and Tuesday. Enter it into attached calculator. Entry is set to 15% of the highest high. SL is set to 10% on the other side of the low for long; high for short. TP is set to 50% of the range. If trade doesn't open by the end of the week, delete pending orders. For example, this week on GBPUSD.Tuesday formed the high; Monday the low I set a buy order at 1.31011. SL was 1.29495 TP was 1.31617 I set a sell and a buy order on each pair. Once one order is opened, delete the other.

Buy order was opened on Wednesday and closed on Friday.

I've manually backtested it on GBPJPY, GBPUSD, GBPAUD for years and it looks good.

Attached is the Day of week indicator I found here on FF. I'd set the indicator to only show MoTu.

ProblemsIf the trend is overextended, it can enter and then get stopped out. In those cases, only consider a pullback. So, the system needs to be refined to take into account the weekly and monthly ATR. If the weekly or the monthly range is already above average, the trade may fail. If the MoTu range is too small, you may not want to set a order that week or you may increase the entry percentage. I'll try to post my trades here, once they close. Any advice would be appreciated.

--- 帖子 #21 ---
Slingshots1, you take whichever is the highest high. So, compare the two highs of Monday and Tuesday and ask, "Which one is higher?" Use that one.

Then ask, "Which low is lower, Monday or Tuesday?" Use that low.

On the example you're referring to, Monday was the higher high and Tuesday was the lower low.

--- 帖子 #39 ---
OK, early figures on GU going back to 27 May 2019, 36 weeks.

Losses - 2

Wins - 18 [+900%]

No trade (range over 200) - 7

Trades with entry totals - 9. for +51pips [+61%] & -124pips [-83%].

% relates to per trade numbers. i.e.: If range equals 100 pips, and trade wins, it has reached 50% of the range. One win =50%.

Losses are dependent on where you decide to place your stop. If stop is 10% beyond opposite side of range, then the loss is =125%

The pip count doesn't matter. This is all about %. Since I'm in US, I have limited broker choices. I use Oanda Proprietary platform because #1 I trust Oanda. #2 Oanda allows trades of any size. If you don't want to trade units of 1,000, you could choose 750 or 1550, basically any size you want. Making it much easier to trade with the exact risk on each trade, regardless of your account size.

--- 帖子 #41 ---
+++++++++++++++++++++++++

Using Oanda, you can place opposing trades, as you can on all brokers I'm aware of. As noted, you would need to manually close one order once you have opposite entry.

Before FIFO (first in first out), you were able to place OCO (One Cancels the Other) trades, so you would not need to manually cancel opposite order.

Kind of confusing, so let me break it down:

• Trades with Entry, refers to all trades entered that did not reach TP or SL.

• I further broke down those in both pips & % based on fib levels.

• Also these trades were measured by taking price at close of Friday. This could be different for each of us, depending on how you decide to manage.

--- 帖子 #44 ---
Ok, here it is. A very basic version just to see if I understood all the rules correctly because english is not my primary language and I'm still new in this (less than 1 year in forex)

What the EA is doing:

-When Tuesday ends and the daily bar closes it will put 1 buystop order and 1 sellstop order and set the TP and SL according to the input percentages of the range between the high and low of Monday+Tuesday. This will do it only if there was no other operation already with the magic number for the day.

-When one of the two pending orders opens it will cancel the other pending order

-On Friday it will delete any pending order

What the EA is not doing

-Closing any order even if it was open for months as the OP didn't give directions for this

-Trailing stop (I can add this feature if needed)

-Money management (Same)

Please test it and point any bugs you may find and of course feel free to modify it as you please but only only and only if you are going to share your work with the rest of us

Cheers!

--- 帖子 #46 ---
+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Thank You. Good job.

One thing to be aware of, some brokers have a different end of day time. In this case there could be SIX daily bars, instead of FIVE.

Five PM New York time (2200 GMT) would give you 5 daily bars. This would change during those times of the year that when your zone may have some sort of Daylight Saving.

--- 帖子 #47 ---
Just finished backtesting 2019, with first 4 weeks of 2020. GbpUsd ONLY!

Criteria:

• 15% Breach of Monday Tuesday Range.

• Profit @ 65% of range.

• Loss @ 80%* retrace of range (= to loss of 95% of total range). Other Stop Losses have been suggested in this thread.

• No Win, No Loss trades closed @ market closing on Friday. This may not be the best way to finish for week.

• No Trades when range is too large. I used 150 pips for this range. Basically double the ADR for GU.

All totals are in % only. % is based on Fibonacci Range of Monday, Tuesday Ranges, NOT Account %!

Final total for 56 weeks, +920%.

• 27 Wins

• 4 Losses

• 15 No Trades because of Range being Too Large

• No Win, No Loss trades, are figured in grand total

* Suggested Stop Loss of 10% opposite side of range (-125%), would have been hit on all 4 losses I recorded.

--- 帖子 #50 ---
Sangui, thanks for the EA! Some thoughts...

Number 5 below may be an error?

1. Option to keep the opposite pending order open even if it opens to the other side. Many times the other trade would help alleviate some lose.

2. Can we allow for trading on Friday? In my system, anyway, I allow for trades on Friday. The pending orders should be deleted at Friday close, not Friday open. Maybe an option to open on Fridays or not?

3. Motu Maximum Range of the Weekly ATR. Explained/Formula: MoTu range times _____ (option, e.g., .75) must be less than Weekly ATR 14 period to open trade.

4. Maximum monthly range percentage. If the present month has already reached ______ (option, e.g., .75) of the previous months ATR 14 reading, do not open. For example, the trade on 2019.02.27. February had already reached a range of about 515. The previous months ATR was 533. Therefore, if this was set to .95, the trade would not have opened.

5. On mine, 2019.03.20 has a deleted sell order. It should have stayed open. Did that happen for you?

That should suffice. I really appreciate your contribution, Sangui! Much appreciated!

3-4. I guess it's possible but it will take me a little more time because they act on different timeframes so I think the only way is by editing, substracting and modifying the indicator's code. If someone else knows how to do it quickly please go ahead.

Don't you think that this functionality will filter too many good trades?

5. What happened here is that two rules were contradicting. A buy order was opened on the previous week but didn't hit TP or SL, so when it sets the buystop and the sellstop on Wednesday it deletes the sellstop inmidiately as we already have an opposite order open. I changed it to compare only with the current week orders and now it works fine. Good catch!

--- 帖子 #64 ---
Hello to all

First of all, please excuse my English which is not my mother tongue, thankfully there is google translation ...

Quoting 4ecstasy

Indeed, it is necessary to add (or subtract in the event of a sale) to the 50% of the range the 15% difference with the highest when taking a position.

2 lines of code must therefore be modified :
Inserted Code double buyTP = NormalizeDouble(high + range * takeProfitPercentage / 100, 5);
double sellTP = NormalizeDouble(low - range * takeProfitPercentage / 100, 5);
become
Inserted Code double buyTP = NormalizeDouble((buyPrice-high)+high + range * takeProfitPercentage / 100, 5);
double sellTP = NormalizeDouble(low - range * takeProfitPercentage / 100-(low-sellPrice), 5);

Here is the modified EA

--- 帖子 #78 ---
Nice testing guys.

Degolep, if you want to use it for XAUUSD you will need to replace the 5s for 2s in the NormalizeDouble funtion calls:
Inserted Code    double buyPrice = NormalizeDouble(high + range * entryRangePercentage / 100, 2);
double sellPrice = NormalizeDouble(low - range * entryRangePercentage / 100, 2);
double buyTP = NormalizeDouble((buyPrice-high)+high + range * takeProfitPercentage / 100, 2);
double sellTP = NormalizeDouble(low - range * takeProfitPercentage / 100-(low-sellPrice), 2);
double buySL = NormalizeDouble(low - range * stopLossPercentage / 100, 2);
double sellSL = NormalizeDouble(high + range * stopLossPercentage / 100, 2);

Nevermind, found a way to make it work for every pair.

--- 帖子 #90 ---
I'm convinced that we need to take into account the recent trend. If it's too strong, it could go against us.

If the range of the last week or so   is significantly greater than the ATR 14 period, I wouldn't open it. But this needs testing!

More of a formula: For long, if Bar 1 is greater than bar ...say ... bar 8 by 1.5 times ATR 14, then the trend is overextended and shouldn't be considered.

--- 帖子 #132 ---
TBH knowing how the Fibonacci Tool plots values is basic math.

The 2 points in the settings are "0" and "1"  When the Tool is applied to the chart, the distance between these points is the range.

Say the range is exactly 100 pips, the retracement and extension settings will reflect that. For example, the setting of 1.25 or -0.25 will plot the lines 25 pips from the "1" and "0" lines of the high and low.

For me, the logic of using the Fibonacci Tool to plot the Monday Tuesday HIGH to LOW,  lies in the fact that the Entry is plotted to a percentage of that range, rather than an arbitrary fixed number of pips for every pair. In other words, it changes with the volatility of the pair.

Using the example above, when the range is doubled to 200 pips, the Entry is also doubled to 50 pips, compared to the fixed model of say 15 which would be the same for both pairs.

Just depends on how you view price action, myself, I see that every pair has different Average Daily Range so think this should be considered when deciding on entry and target points.

You're on to something.

You know you can implement this, from beginning of the week phase to an hourly chart? Or daily, whatever.

It's the same concept statistically:

price will move to be ~10% on one side, before it will go to about 5x to the opposite side, 80% of the time, to create the normal range; in a blink of an eye no less. :-)

Of course, that 10% isn't just for it to be there, you ever know how much crap a bank can fit in an hour's, day's, week's time? More advertisement than an American football game.

Heck, even if the fake move is 1%

1%+ the spread that many times will not be enough to cover the 5x reward. It's like gambling still if you made it this far... needs refinement.

Add a bit of a low blow by not finishing a range, and people are triggered not following discipline, changing systems, fading prices, omens, psychology, magic number trails, entering at high volatility and card reading(order flow & candle types) for prediction purposes.

Just complete GU analysis for 2016. Using 65% as TP & 70% as SL. Making R:R 17:10.

Here's what I found:

• 23 Wins = +1150%

• 8 Losses = -680%  None Consecutive

• 15 weeks with no trade. Since the GU was more active in 2016, ranges larger than 200 pips, were not traded. Brexit crap.

• The weeks which were entered without hitting SL or TP, ended up slightly negative.

By doubling your trade size following a loss, the -680% would change into +120%.

By making your % = to $1 each, that would have netted about $45/week.

** Remember, percentage is equal to fibonacci % per trade, so you would need to figure your risk per trade for results in currency.

--- 帖子 #160 ---
Total range is taken from the Highest High and Lowest Low of Monday and Tuesday candles

If they are both on the same candle it is OK, then that is your total range, so in your chart Monday is engulfing Tuesday candle

Put your FIB tool or range box on with your desired settings or you can use the OP's settings from Post 1, I am using them in my chart example except I am using TP at 165%

Hello to all

Quoting  Fantuz

Yes of course. This closes all the positions when the account shows a gain or a loss of what you have defined in the table. It is not in pips but in account money.

--- 帖子 #187 ---
Not a silly question, but your answer is in the question.

The descriptions you used for candles, there is only 1 high, 1 open, 1 low and 1 close price.

Therefore the very ends of the wicks are the high or the low; the bodies are from open to close.

Take a close look at the charts I have posted, see the High and Low marked by the lines of the Fibonacci Tool.

Good luck, hope you stick around, come back for more

--- 帖子 #191 ---
Hi 4ecstacy & Sangui,

4ecstacy - Thank you for starting this discussion & sharing your ideas.

Sangui - Thank you for your work creating the EA and sharing with the group.

erebus - Thank you for sharing your experience, insights and humor.

Rereading the third sentence in Post #1,
"Logic behind the system: The highs and lows of Monday and Tuesday often form the low or the high of the week."

I have been considering how it works trading as daily breakout from previous day's range.

From the statement above, Tuesday has very high probability of being higher or lower than Monday's range. Why not trade Tuesday as breakout too?

Same thing for Wednesday vs Tuesday's range, Thursday vs Wednesday's range, etc.

Manually testing daily breakout with Fibo using erebus settings: Hi & Low Entry = 0%, TP = 25%, SL = 50%, high percentage of days are winners.

You can quickly test this with Fibo using erebus settings: Hi & Low Entry = 0%, TP = 25%, SL = 50%, and walk it through any days and weeks in history.

Sangui, for testing, is it possible to modify the EA to trade every day vs the previous day's range? Mon vs Fri, Tue vs Mon, Wed vs Tue, etc?

Primary enhancement request is for trading every day.

This second request is for possible later improvement if EA works for trading every day.

The other addition to the EA would be to have ability to place multiple Buy-Stop & Sell-Stop trades, at same Hi/Low Entry = 0%, with TP at #1=25%, #2=50%, #3=100% (user select %s).

When position #1 hits TP at 25%, move position #2 & #3 SL to 5% or 10%.

When/if #2 hits TP at 50%, move position #3 SL to 25%.

A footnote to the request for opening multiple trades, for folks in the USA, EA will have to change the lot size and/or entry price for each order.

For example:

Lot size change: #1 = 0.13 lots, #2 = 0.12 lots, #3 = 0.11 lots.

Entry Price change: #1 = 1.12303, #2 = 1.12304, #2 = 1.12305.

Once again, thank you for your consideration, and thank you for what looks like a great idea.

All the best,

John

--- 帖子 #214 ---
This is why an EA is not ideal with such a system. In fact, EAs usually don't work in favor of the trader in the long run. Nothing beats trading manually. There are certain things to look out for such as volume, overall strength of trend and strength of currency, proximity to major support or resistance, etc...  An EA can only do so much.

The best kind of EAs to use are money management/trade management EA's. But having EAs do all your trading for you is not the wisest approach to trading, as it will most likely lead to more losses than wins.

I think this is a great system, and likely would work out in the long run. But I believe it has to be done manually, because not all market conditions will work in harmony with such a strategy.

--- 帖子 #232 ---
I maked a simple script(not EA) for this actions.

On first wednesday's H1 bar I drag-n-drop script on the chart. And repeat it for all currencies charts.

What script will do: check for highest high and lowest low for last 48 H1 bars and send 2 pending orders - buy stop & sell stop by %fibo setted when script loaded.

Example for lvl_for_enter = 25:

Entry level for buy stop order = 125% fibo at range

Entry level for sell stop order = -25% fibo at range

Example for sl_for_order = 25:

StopLoss level for buy order = High of range - 25% = 75% fibo

StopLoss level for sell order = Low of range + 25% = 25% fibo

tp: for 5 digits brokers - multuply by 10

if tp = 0, orders need to close manuality.

I close all orders few hours before market close at friday.

Here is my problem. I am bound by FIFO and 'no hedge' rules. So I can't set orders up like that. It's more of a trade management EA.

Having said that, what I meant about a scanner is having an additional condition to detect higher probability trading setups for this strategy. For example, a trend filter might be useful or a combination of that and something else. The scanner can be placed on a single chart and monitor all 28 pairs or whatever amount the user desires, and locate these higher probability setups. Once identified, a signal will be given to the user who will then decide whether to set up the trade or not or to select the currency pair(s) he or she wants to use at that time.

I have not experimented with this strategy long enough to know what other conditions might be useful in this regard.

--- 帖子 #235 ---
Just an idea, but if a person implementing this strategy uses a trend bias from a higher time frame such as the Daily or Weekly, it might be in his or her best interest to double up the risk on pending orders leaning in the direction of the trend, within reason, of course.

In other words, let's say the trend is strong bullish. That would mean there is a higher probability it will breakout to the upside. So a trader could place a buy pending order in favor of the trend at 0.10 while placing a sell pending order in opposite direction to the trend at 0.05. This could potentially minimize the risk and make up for losses. A break even strategy might even be useful.

Strategy refinement to work towards producing the best possible outcome can be of great benefit.

Note: This is just an idea for educational purposes. Not financial advice. You trade at your own risk.

Hi all,

First off, thank you 4ecstasy for the system - it looks very good, and I've missed this week, but will be giving it a go next week.

I was wondering if anyone has thought about whether or not broker server times make any difference to the strategy?  I think that brokers who are well off from GMT would have a big impact on the strategy, but those that are +/- 1 or 2 may not.

The answer to this would, of course be to use H1 to determine the high & low of Monday and Tuesday, adjusted according to the broker's offset.

e.g. my broker is IC Markets, and is GMT+2, meaning that their daily candle starts at 22:00 GMT.  So, using H1, I would use 02:00 Monday to 02:00 Wednesday to get the upper and lower limits.

It's only 2 hours, I know, but I'm wondering if it could have a big impact?

--- 帖子 #275 ---
Dynamic means moving

Static means stopped

In the context of trades, dynamic means the pip count or profit is still moving as the trades are still open.

When trades are closed, the pip count or profit will remain fixed or static.

Your English lesson for the week

Lessons from “the Turtles”

1) Trade with an edge. Find a strategy that brings profits in the long-term.

2) Manage your risks. Manage your risks to stay in the game longer and enjoy a winning streak.

3) Be consistent. Follow the entry rules to reach your goal and earn a profit.

4) Keep it simple. Simple trading systems tend to be more reliable and time-tested.

--- 帖子 #369 ---
No, not pips, percentage

The Fibonacci Tool has a range of 0 to 1, in the settings

These are the points when drawing the Fibs from High to Low

The range between high and low, between 0 to 1, could be anything, but it's 100%

So, a setting of 1.15 and -0.15 will draw a line 15% away from the 0 line and the 1 line

Every pair will be different, the greater the range between high and low,  the greater the distance between the 0 line and the -0.15 line, same for the 1 line and the 1.15 line.

Automatically adjusts for volatility

Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #370 ---

--- 帖子 #385 ---
If anyone is having trouble drawing the lines, use this as a guide.

Print the Following Images for Easy Reference (provided by Erebus)

Image 1: https://www.forexfactory.com/attachm...3&d=1581757757

Image 2: https://www.forexfactory.com/attachm...4&d=1581757765

Remember: positive numbers go on top and negative numbers go on the bottom in the Fibs tool

When using the Fibs tool, be sure to go from the top to the bottom on the chart to make everything appear in its correct order.

Source: https://www.forexfactory.com/showthr...3#post12756303

--- 帖子 #421 ---
So I have an idea for an EA. Tell me what you think about these rules. The idea is to keep it simple.

EA for Previous 2 Days

Settings:

1. Trigger Lines: EA will automatically draw lines on chart at the high and the low of the previous two days. One line for a Buy order and one line for Sell order.

Note: This will only work once.

2. Market Orders: When a candle hits either one of the Trigger Lines, a market order will be placed and the remaining inactive Trigger Line will be automatically deleted

3. Pips Above/Below: User may input a pip amount to work in cooperation with the Trigger Lines. For example, if user inputs 25 pips, then a sell trade will only open if a candle hits the 25 pip mark beyond the sell trigger line, and vice versa for buy trades. If this setting is 0, then it will be disabled.

3. Maximum Allowed Spread: EA will not place trades above the max spread, as specified by user in pips. For example, if it's 5 pips, then only a spread of 5 pips or less will be allowed. Anything above this will be rejected.

4. Stop Loss

5. 50% Off: half of trade will close at user's specified pip amount (can be set to true or false)

6. Magic Number

7. Direction:

a. Default - will only follow settings 1 and 2

b. Long - will only execute long trades (trigger line will only be drawn at the high of the previous two days)

c. Short - will only execute short trades (trigger line will only be drawn at the low of the previous two days)

8. Take Profit: will continue to run if set to 0

9. Manual Mode: if set to true, user may manually input specific prices to open buy or sell trades.

10. Break Even (if 0, then break even will be disabled) Note: both Break Even and 50% off must work together if user has both settings enabled.

I cannot code this. It's just an idea I came up with. If we can get an expert coder to create this EA (without putting unreasonable user limitations on it), then that would be great.

If you think it can be improved, then please share your thoughts.

--- 帖子 #470 ---
Welcome to the matrix

There are 8 “main” Currencies = AUD, CAD, CHF, EUR, GBP, JPY, NZD, USD

Anything with USD is called a Major, 7 pairs

USDCAD;USDCHF;USDJPY;AUDUSD;EURUSD;GBPUSD;NZDUSD

When the others are crossed, they are called Minor, 21 pairs, total of 28 pairs

Some pairs don’t make sense most of the time, AUDNZD, too close related, like kissing your sister

And EURCHF, get out of here, kissing first cousin, same for EURGBP

And CHFJPY, both safe haven currency, can be frustrating

Good luck, and pucker up

--- 帖子 #480 ---
Just an observation that may help others...

I've noticed that most of the trades that I currently have running negative (including the full loss on GBPNZD) were false breakouts.

Had I not entered exactly on the entry line (+15% of the range for me), but instead went to a lower timeframe for the entry (say M15) and then only entered when the price broke and CLOSED above the trigger line, I would not have opened any of the negative trades.

--- 帖子 #623 ---
My EA Idea Updated

(previous version)

Note: You are FREE to create an EA using the following recipe. But please keep in mind that it is my EA recipe. As the copyright owner of this recipe, my rules are simple: any EA created using the following recipe must be FREE to edit, FREE to use, FREE from user restrictions, and may not be used for commercial purposes.

This EA recipe is my contribution to this community.

EA for 2 Day Breakout

Settings:

1. Trigger Lines: EA will automatically draw lines on chart at the high and the low of the previous two days. One line for a Buy order and one line for Sell order. User can limit this by only allowing the EA to do this for a specific set of days, such as Monday and Tuesday, for example. Only one trade will be allowed at a time per currency pair.

2. Market Orders: When a candle hits either one of the Trigger Lines, a market order will be placed and the untouched Trigger Line will be deleted

3. Pips or Percent Above/Below: User may input a pip amount to work in cooperation with the Trigger Lines. For example, if user inputs 25 pips, then a sell trade will only open if a candle hits the 25 pip mark beyond the sell trigger line, and vice versa for buy trades. This may be set in percent rather than pips. If this setting is 0, then it will be disabled.

4. Maximum Allowed Spread: EA will not place trades above the max spread, as specified by user in pips. For example, if it's 5 pips, then only a spread of 5 pips or less will be allowed. Anything above this will be rejected.

5. Stop Loss: may be by pips or a specific price. If it is by price, then an additional option may be enabled for candle body close stop loss.

6. 50% Off: half of trade will close at user's specified pip amount (can be set to true or false)

7. Magic Number

8. Direction:

a. Default - will only follow settings 1 and 2

b. Long - will only execute long trades (trigger line will only be drawn at the high of the previous two days)

c. Short - will only execute short trades (trigger line will only be drawn at the low of the previous two days)

9. Take Profit: will continue to run if set to 0

10. Manual Mode: if set to true, user may manually input price values

11. Break Even (if 0, then break even will be disabled) Note: both Break Even and 50% off must work together if user has both settings enabled.

12. Option to choose currency pairs.

Note: this recipe does not rely on the OP's strategy. It is much more than that! If the OP's strategy ceases to work, my recipe will continue to work, because it is mostly a trade management recipe, based on a breakout/market order trading system.

--- 帖子 #632 ---
Well i took my time and learned some MQL 5 my self... With some very little tweeking to the code and some "include" files we can use the script in MT5, just as in MT4.

Quick guide:

- Place the "mq4_mq5_bridge.mqh" file in .../MQL5/Include/" folder

- Place script in ".../MQL5/Scripts/" folder

- Load MT5

- Drag and drop script to chart or add a hotkey (for faster use).

It wont work without the "mq4_mq5_bridge.mqh" file. its the one that makes the magic happend and translate the MQL4 expressions to MQL5...

Since marked its closed, i cant test it yet. Ill wait for monday... Atleast not what i am aware about

My the pips be with you.

--- 帖子 #641 ---
I know you think you know I don't own the rights to my EA recipe, but you are misinformed.

As a copyright lawyer, you should know that as soon a creative work is created, it is copyrighted by default, according to US copyright law. Unless its creator clearly states it belongs to the public domain.

I am very familiar with copyright law as I have had dealings with it on several occasions from people whom I had to file a DMCA against for attempting to steal written works from me and passing them off as their own.

If someone hires you to create an EA based on their trading recipe, then it's your code that is copyrighted. You have no rights to the idea (recipe) itself. It's not yours. You didn't create it. The person who created the recipe has full rights to it, and you must have that person's permission to use it, and if permission is given to you to use it, you must abide by the creator's terms of use or not use it.

--- 帖子 #647 ---
That's all I want. As long as it is in the spirit of giving, you are free to use the trading management recipe I shared here.

I just don't want people using my idea to take advantage of others or to profit from it commercially. That wouldn't be right, since it is meant to be FREE.

I will still hire the coder I am communicating with to create the EA, as he is a highly skilled coder whose work I have come to trust.

The bulk of the recipe came about as a result of many hours spent trading the Forex market. The rules require more than just putting up an EA on a chart and hoping things will work out for the best. It still requires a degree of technical analysis on the part of the user to know which rules to apply, where to apply them, and when to implement them. I even have a specially designed stop loss in there to deal with stop loss spikes (stop hunting) which often occur in the market.

The rules are formulated in such a way that the EA containing them can work with or without the OP's strategy. That makes it very powerful! As you are likely aware, EAs that are purely based on a specific strategy usually stop working at some point. To keep that from happening, my idea places more weight on the trade management side.

It even has rules to deal with FIFO and no hedging rules, which US citizens are unfairly subject to.

The only way the recipe will stop working is if the EA becomes outdated and isn't updated or if people are no longer allowed to trade using EAs. Otherwise, it is timeless.

--- 帖子 #648 ---
OK, so here is the thing with me. I am a visual person. I need to see the rules/settings in a script/EA and have some kind of control over which ones I want to use and when.

It's Ok if people just want to put up a script and let the script do everything for them. But how long will that work? That question remains unanswered. My recipe, on the other hand, should always work. Whether it will be profitable or not depends on the decisions the user makes while using it. Success all depends on the conditions of the market and the user's knowledge of how to trade it.

I'm sorry to disagree with you, but it seems that you are the one who is misinformed here.

Sure, if you create an EA (or get someone to create an EA for you) then you may own the copyright for that EA, i.e. no-one is permitted to sell, modify or distribute the EA without your express permission, but you do NOT own the copyright to the "recipe", as you put it, for two very good reasons:You cannot copyright an idea.  You can patent a design, but you cannot copyright an idea. Pretty much every one of the features that you have listed for your EA are already features in other EAs that are available in the public domain - they are not unique to you.  Heck, even my own EAs do most of what you've specified, and I wrote the code for those over the last couple of years...so by your logic, perhaps you owe me something for copyright infringement?

Hi All,

One EA to place all trades required on Wednesday morning.  Each pair NEEDS ITS OWN CHART with the EA on it.

The system also creates Global Variables found under Tools.  This is to stop multiple entries and other stuff.  If you want to try it multiple times then delete the variable DrawHiLo and corresponding PAIR number.  Probably better just to try it on one or two charts then set up for Wenesday with the ones you want to trade.

The PAIR numbers do not correspond to your charts they are the numbers in the list below.

DEMO TRADING IS RECOMMENDED TO START I will not be held responsible for any errors or ommisions or any losses that you may incur.

I have modified my existing Basic system which I use for testing ideas and tested it as much as I can today.  It seems to be ok.

If you want to try it today change DayStart to 1.  It is set to default to 3 for Wednesday.

As I am only providing an .EXE , for various reasons, at this stage this is NOT modifiable.

I have a TradeManagement routine incorporated which at the moment is blocked off so we can think about that next version or so.

Attached File(s)   EA Daily Mon Tues  v1.0.ex4

20 KB
|
191 downloads

I said I would use version numbers then realised you would have to go through the laborious task of re-adding to each chart.

There have been a few challenges in opening 52 simultaneous orders and I can't say I am 100% happy with the solution, although it certainly works.

Also once you have a Pending order for both Long and Short all you can do is wait for a break to go live.  You have therefore no further control, other than manual deleting the order, to decide if the break is real or if there is any trend or price has reached a resistance point ,pivots etc,etc. You name it its all out there.

This is what makes developing an EA very useful.  You have to think of ALL the eventualities because the computer won't do it for you and "rules is rules".

I'll leave it as it is for now and those interested in trying it can do so and we can think if this is the best way forward.   I am going to diverge slightly as I can code the differences in and use a another method of breakout.  I will let you know.

--- 帖子 #788 ---
Hi Mohsen-b,

I didn't continue developing the EA and didn't test what you say but with a quick look at the code I can see that I am checking for symbol in the IfOneSideOpenedCancelTheOther() function:

if(OrderMagicNumber() == MagicNumber && OrderSymbol() == Symbol()...

So I don't know why that would be happening.

You can try adding this line in the OnInit() to create a unique MN for every time you attach the EA: MagicNumber = WindowHandle(Symbol(),0);

If you do that also change the input MagicNumber by extern int MagicNumber;

About editing the parameters while the EA is running I didn't even know that was possible to be honest.

--- 帖子 #883 ---
For gauging the true profitability it's best to ignore pips and concentrate on the % profit.

If you've used fixed lots for every pair, you need to work out how many 1:1 wins and 1:1 losses you have had.

For example, in your case, it looks like you had 5 wins, 1 loss and 3 roughly break-even. So all told, you're looking at 4% gain for the week if you'd risked 1% per trade...pretty good!

--- 帖子 #909 ---
Please note what he said - TP is 100 points

If and when you understand the Fibonacci Tool, it doesn’t calculate in pips but Percentage

Therefore, a 1 to 1 Take Profit of the “range” measured from Entry to 50% stop loss, will be exactly that same number of pips

On your chart, the prices - High Entry 1.34593 - Stop Loss 1.33760 = 0.00833 pips (notice, NOT 100 pips)

Add that to the High Entry 1.34593 + 0.00833 = 1.35426 which is exactly what is on your chart

Another thing for you to check, the accurate placement of the Fibonacci Tool to the actual high and low

I suggest drop down to the 1-hour chart to see this in fine details

Study the charts below, cheers

We are not mind readers, but let’s assume that you are using Metatrader 4

When placing a pending order, the options are there to include the take profit and stop loss price also

When you place the order, it is held on the brokers server, you can turn off your computer.

I suggest that you read the User Manual, very throughly, okay?

And don’t believe random people on the forums, take responsibility

--- 帖子 #926 ---
TP was set at 100 just to get something on the chart.

When using a PC to set up trades rather than a tablet it's easier to move SL & TP to where you really want them. On screen drag and drop, especially the latter.

This strategy is based on the price action of Monday and Tuesday, that's fair enough. The MM, to me, is a wet finger in the air, apologies to OP, with no consideration of likely support, resistance when setting SL & tp. To me the exit is the most important part of any strategy and shouldn't be nieve or contrived.

Set the orders and then manage the stops accordingly.

As an example  I have a couple of strategies that are intraday. I know that the open plus the daily atr is a good place for TP. A high percent of days price will stick around this value.  Not all, some don't reach some go past, but as a rule of thumb for an unmanaged trade it is a good point. This is not nieve or contrived but analysed.

I could go on.

I'm happy to put the defaults into the ea for those that can use it plus other requests but I recommend that are a starting point.

The other area is position sizing which I hope to add shortly.

Trailing stop, at the moment I don't have any view. I don't really like them, I prefer to manage trades from a lower tf.

--- 帖子 #945 ---
I think this method should be traded as a "basket" or "notabasket" as Erebus puts it. Either way, I think if we trade a number of pairs and set individual TP's and SL's on each just as we are now, but also have an overall TP% for the "notabasket" If any pair hit's their individual TP and the overall % has not reached our set TP% then we let all the pairs remain open.....but once the overall basket reaches our set TP% or SL% then we close everything at once. If you wanted I guess you could close all of them except for the strongest trending pair or one that you feel you can get more profit out of, but in the long run I think doing this might bite you in the butt. Setting a TP% for the week imo is the way to go. Really no need to be going for +50% profit from 28 pairs each week.....2.5%/week overall is plenty!

--- 帖子 #951 ---
Because I’m a “trend” trader

You must have seen at least one situation where it prevented a loss, or is it pure conjecture from other methods?

[quote=zoraxfx;12798247]@ transmat many thx for your contribution this system sounds good Strategy Tester Report MoTu_System_v1.4_Close_Friday GlobalPrime-Demo (Build 1260) SymboleEURUSD ]

Thank you zoraxfx but the real designer of the EA is sangui (see in the first posts).

I only added a few lines of code to close the current trade on Friday if desired.

However, I draw attention to a few points:

The backtest presented is attractive but the stoploss is not positioned on Hi Lo / 2 and displaying 100 for the TP, it does not respect the RR 2:1

For the stoploss, do not forget to display the minus sign (-) in front of 50.

I put 130 for the TP because the entry being at 15% of the box it is necessary to add them to the value of the stoploss which is here 50 (in%) the whole multiply by two to obtain RR 2:1.

If you want to enter with 25% you will have to display 150.

The results on the eurusd will be less spectacular but the DD will be lower.

We could therefore increase the size of the position to 0.15 and it will give this:

--- 帖子 #1006 ---
I really want to remind everyone who is waiting for the appearance of new EA here. As you can see, they work on the principle of "day of week = 3" - this is wednesday, closing all orders on friday is "day of week = 5", with hours to close or open orders is the same things.

This is not cleary right when you start testing it in the strategy tester. There are holidays on the market.

For example, there may be no open market on wednesday at all, only monday, tuesday, thursday and friday. And It happens that there is no friday, i.e. the EA will not close orders on friday, because friday as market day can be absolutly absent. Or market may close earlier on friday, and if you decide to use setting for close orders 1 hour before market closes on friday, you may get into a very unpleasant story.

Please be careful when using EA and when you are testing strategies. This can significantly distort the results in one direction or the other.

So if, High is  = 1 and Buy Entry = High +0.15, we get = +1.15

Therefore, Buy Entry to 50% = 0.65

Add 0.65 to 1.15 = +1.80

So if, Low is = 0 and Sell Entry = Low -0.15, we get = -0.15

Therefore, Sell Entry to 50% = 0.65

Subtract 0.65 from -0.15 = -_____

Attached File(s)   EA Daily Mon Tues  v1.0.ex4

I have tested many times and it looks ok.

The button CloseALL does exactly that. ALL trades will be closed.

Trades will open it may take a few seconds minutes depending on how many charts etc. If you put the EA up overnight it should all be working tomorrow.

There is a mechanism which stops multiple trades occurring during the week if you were to test and/or close early. In the GlobalVariables each pair has a number and a value. OpenLongTime is the Weekly time similar for short. There is some duplication here with LongOpened etc but that doesn't affect the way teh EA works. I will look to remove this next versions.

I was going to add an option to specify What Day/ What Hour to close but setting that up requires the user to enter a GlobalVariable. It can be done if anyone wants it and knows how to access through Tools menu. For now its the button.

I won't have time to develop and test position sizing and basket closing but will do that next. The spec will be a configurable % of Account Balance etc. I'm also looking at SET files, never used them but I think Globals are easier to use. They re right there every time on the menu under Tools. Yes I know I have repeated that.

As always please test on a demo chart(s) always better to use 3 or 4 to check for any errors before tomorrow. Don't forget to set and reset startdate to reflect its not yet Wednesday. e.g set to 2 and then back to 3 when finished.

May have been a bit pedantic but just making sure I pass all the info over.

Good Luck

--- 帖子 #1042 ---
Howdy,

Erebus guided me to this thread, and his passion for this trading method was over 9000 - I checked it out and decided to make some tools for him ready for when he gets his computer going.

For me - it is 2 birds with one stone, as I have an extensive trade library that I needed to do some work on, so I used this trading strategy as a "guinea pig" for developing the library - since it is nice and mechanical.

There seems to be some EA's n things being passed around in this thread, so I am a bit late to the party, but to my understanding most of the tools are for MT4.

My contribution today is for MT5. I can compile these to MT4 as well, but I don't want to step on anyone's toes here since I can see SpikeHunter already put something together.

Erebus refers to this method as the WTF method (Wed, Tues, Something something) ... so I just stuck with that.

The indicator: WTF Helper.ex5

Will mark the mon-tues high low levels from Wednesday. Works on all time frames.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

There is a simple candle marker that you can turn on/off. It will mark candles that close on one side of the channel and close on the other... indicating a possible Mon-Tues breakout.

Just a nice quick visual aid.

The Expert: WTFTrader.ex5

As I mentioned earlier, I was using this system to work on a trade library that has a lot of tools in it. So I've included quite a bit for you to play around with.

Entry Stuff: The robot will not set pending orders, it will wait until price touches the breakout trigger level (from Wednesdays onward) then open an order on touch. It will only have one trade open at a time per pair. If a trade fails, it will still allow one more trade to be triggered in the opposite direction. So basically you get one trade trigger per direction. At the end of the week it resets internal counters. But be careful here, I haven't fully optimized this to remember its state if you unload the ea and then reload it. It will see open trades that it placed before, and work off that basis, but otherwise unloading and re-loading the EA will mean a "reset" of the internal trade counters in most cases.

I didn't really polish this aspect because I was mainly flogging this in the back-tester, checking the things I was implementing, were working as intended.

There was also some discussion here about having a buffer outside the channel boundary.

Add_Entry_Threashold Is the entry buffer setting. 0.1 = 10%, which will add 10% of the Mon-Tue range to the entry condition.

During back testing I noticed that timing was swinging results wildly. So Trade_Hour_Start and Trade_Hour_End are the hours which the EA will be allowed to place trades. It's set to 8-15 by default which were showing the best results on my broker.

These times work off your broker hour, so when your broker hour hits London Open is a ballpark time when you want to allow trading. Play around with this in the back tester. Just put 0 - 23 to essentially allow trading in all hours.

Stop Loss Calculations:

Here you will start to see all the options my trade library is offering.

There are two stop loss selections. One selection are standard / generic kind of stop loss methods, and the other one is stop loss methods that are unique to this strategy only.

To use the stop loss method unique to this strategy,Set Stop_Strategy to: STOP_LOSS_USE_STRATEGY_METHOD Select a stop loss method from System_Stop_Loss_Method (I only have one in there at the moment) The option WTF_STOPLOSS_MON_TUE_CHAN_PCT will set the trade stop loss at a percentage point of the monday - tues channel. By the amount set in Stop_Strategy_Value

Careful: It is expecting decimals here... 0.5 = 50% of the candle.

Otherwise you can use my built in stop loss methods. Eg.Stop loss by prev candle high/low Stop loss by volatility (atr) - use multiplier to multiples of the atr, eg set stop loss multiplier value to 2 for 2xATR Stop loss by prev swing high/low - Stop_Strategy_Value = fractal value here,  stop loss multiplier adds buffer spacing (remember pct in decimal format)
Trailing Stop MethodsLots to play with here Remember multiplier values are in decimal format Some methods don't use multiplier values, like trail by EMA Min risk reward achieved by trade before trailing kicks in (strongly recommended for some trail methods) Break even conditions
You've also got other options with are pretty straight forwardRisk settings (by account %, or by $ value) Set targets by risk reward multiples Plus some more..

Hopefully that get's you started.

Please don't use this on a live account until you've played around with it on demo and you understand how the input options are working.

Have fun, get well soon Erebus.

--- 帖子 #1067 ---
Here you go buddy (taken from my own EA):
Inserted Code //+------------------------------------------------------------------+
//| Delete all objects for this EA.
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
void DeleteObjects(string objectPrefix)
{
//--- delete all objects
int obj_total=ObjectsTotal();
for(int i=obj_total-1; i>=0; i--)
{
string name=ObjectName(i);
if(StringSubstr(name,0,4)==objectPrefix)
{
ObjectDelete(name);
}
}
}

When you create your objects, simply prefix them with a unique 4-char label. Calling this routine, passing the prefix, will remove them all from the chart.

Use ExpertRemove() to unload the EA from the chart.

--- 帖子 #1081 ---
Instead of a button, why not just provide a bool parameter that the user can set to remove all objects or not?  Much simpler.

Why not use a routine that clears everything?  Because that’s not playing nice with other indicators...a user may use your EA in conjunction with other indicators, so if you remove all object, instead of just those created by your EA, you may cause those indicators to malfunction.  It ‘cleaner’. To remove just those you created.

--- 帖子 #1101 ---
Its a great question.  When does Wednesday start.  Its different for each time zone as a new day starts at midnight and then you have to take into account GMT and your brokers server time. There probably several Wednesday starts.

My EA uses the DayOfWeek function which ranges fro 0 to 6 Sunday to Saturday which I presume is taken by MT4 from the brokers server time.  Wednesday is therefore =3.  There always seem to be discrepancies between systems using different brokers so its a case of doing your own analysis and checking the results are what you want.  Some brokers like mine have open at 22:00 on Sunday so I have 2 Sunday candles.  This really screws up any indicators based on daily prices so I tend to stay away from daily systems.  This one is cleaner in that it is an analysis of Mon & Tues prices what ever they may be and then a break out.  No indicators to get in the way, at the moment at least.

--- 帖子 #1108 ---
Well if you're serious about running a trading robot, you've got to account for these things.

My solution would be to have the EA fully restore its state and "pick up where it left off".

Pending Orders Vs EA Market Order

It depends what you want. Placing pending orders is the easiest "set and forget" method. But I seen you guys are trading a lot of pairs, and on Wednesday your MT4 is blanketed with pending orders on all different markets.

Correct me if I am wrong, but you've got some sort of system in place where if one of the pending orders is triggered, the rest need to be deleted? or cut down in some way.

If that's the case, you nulled your own argument, because you need the EA there to watch those pending orders on every tick to manage which ones are going to get closed off after a trade trigger event.

The "power outage" scenario will screw you either way - I can't imagine that you would just let it place pending orders from all different markets and think you're safe if the EA got cut off. Imagine if they all got triggered, the risk management is still needed with the pending orders approach on some level from the EA.

If there is a power out on a market execution EA during the moment the signal triggers, you miss the trade. If the EA is out with the pending order approach, you could potentially have 20 unwanted trades trigger.

Does that make sense?

--- 帖子 #1159 ---
That would be margin, and has nothing to do with stop loss.

The broker's margin requirements for the instrument worked out that you didn't have enough fund in the account to cover the broker's position. It's pretty standard - on demo too - it simply depends on who the broker is and what's occurring at the time (they can vary margin requirements from day to day).

--- 帖子 #1230 ---
Charts don't get much cleaner than this. I'm going to try to limit the pairs that I trade with this strategy so i'm not risking tooooo much. I'm going to try to risk around .5% to 1% per pair. I'm going to treat these trades as a basket but also let each pair have a set TP and SL. If some of the pairs hit a TP or SL but my overall basket TP or SL hasn't been hit yet, i'll continue to trade. Once the overall basket TP or SL has been hit than I will "close all trades" no matter what. I'm not quite sure what a good overall TP and SL is yet. I haven't had enough time to forward test this strategy. I think I will start with a TP of around 3%-5% and a SL of 5%. These are just a starting point and by no means "set in stone". I'm going to focus on All USD pairs except for USDCHF (not trading CHF) and ALL GBP pairs except for GBPCHF, and EURAUD and EURNZD due to their big ranges.

Okay, here is the chart, the first (smaller) yellow box is where a trade triggered on a pending order - Buy Stop

The red box is where that trade was exited on the Stop Loss order

The second (larger) yellow box is where there is opportunity to re-enter the trade

Both were BUY or LONG trades

GBPCHF is the opposite of EURGBP, please read the article I linked previously.

--- 帖子 #1249 ---
The stop loss you are using appears to be too tight for this strategy.

It is more efficient to use the Average Daily Range as a stop loss.

Had you used the ADR (currently 92 pips for period 10) as a stop loss on your EURGBP trade, you would not have gotten stopped out, and you could have collected pips on this pair up until Friday.

--- 帖子 #1253 ---
So I just did a "visual" back test on this strategy using GBPUSD from March 1st 2019 to Current (52 weeks). Here is what I was using as my criteria. Opening trades at 15% with a 50%SL. Once a trade reaches 50% of the 1:1 target I move the SL to BE. I leave all trades open until either the TP or SL is hit or then end of the trading day on Friday. I don't open any trades on Friday. I only open trades on Wed and Thur. That's pretty much it. Here are my results.....

1:1 was reached 18 times

2:1 was reached 6 times

SL was hit 8 times at 50% of the range

SL was hit 3 times at 100% of the range

No Trade 10 times

Break Even 6 times

Small Loss at close on Friday 4 times

Small Win at close on Friday 6 times

EDIT: If I risked 1% per trade I would have made +18% on the wins and -8% on the losses. That leaves +10%...plus or minus the small wins and losses (6 small wins and 4 small losses).  I know you're probably thinking at first...."this is only +10%+/- for 52 weeks"......BUT.....this is only 1 pair and only 1% per week. If I were trading only 1 pair per week I would most likely risk at least 5%. So you can safely multiply that +10% by 5 if you only wanted to trade this one pair.........now....50%+/- for the last 52 weeks!! Does that sound better?!?

--- 帖子 #1270 ---
Once a BUYSTOP/SELLSTOP order is placed there is no further control available.  This doesn't mean you can't achieve what you want.  You would have to place a market order when the close, I assume a lower timeframe, has happened.  Problem for some with this is that the EA would need to be continuously running and market orders don't always get filled at the level you thought i.e. slippage.  Sometimes not at all "OffQuotes"

I must admit I am not keen on the Pending orders as any old spike can activate them and the idea of a clear breakthrough is my way of thinking, however at the moment I will stick with the current method until I get a clearer idea of the breakout strategy.  Give me you ideas, clearly.

Thank you Spikehunter for your response.

My idea was to have a confirmation over a period in H1 to have a better chance of the start of a lasting trend by a close of the candle beyond or on the entry level.

Of course this requires that the EA is always running (on the PC or on a VPS) and to place it on a graph in H1.

I modified the EA in this sense with this new version.

In the settings, I also changed the stoploss level to at least 55% of the range levels because often a 50% retracement is not uncommon and it's annoying to be kicked out for a few pips.

The RR is always 2: 1 in this setting, but you can change everything.

Test it and tell me what you think.

--- 帖子 #1290 ---
I once read an article from a trading wizard who stated a number of things. The ones relevant here would be:

Simple but not simplistic

A real reason to take a trade (he actually said he looks for reasons NOT to take trades

Direction

Momentum

This latter point to me is especially important as we see to often spikes initiating trades or closing on slwhereas a little more attention to real momentum would keep you out or in. Price isn't always your friend. A close or a number of closes at a lower tf may help. GBPNZD last week proves the point exactly.

This reminds me of the sushi trade by a well known trader, sorry haven't got his name to hand. Price takes out new hi/lo over last 5 bars then reverses and takes a new lo/hi over 5 bars. A reversal price pattern.

There is here a defined idea which if followed looks good to make money.  There isn't much else that can be said that hasn't already been said.  Getting close to a time to spend the cash and move on.

Yes it can have an auto close on Friday at 20:00, see below, and a button top right corner. That's the one I have on my charts. Let me know if the button is there. It is in a fixed position so the screen needs to be wide enough. I cant really fine a place which doesn't obscure it if a user opens up panels or makes the chart small. I recently started using buttons and I am not sure they will float. If you don't want the auto stop just set the Global variable "WhenToStopDay" found under the Tools menu to "0" this will prevent it from closing. If you want to use this feature again check both the Day and Hour are set to what you want. I haven't been able to fully test this only by "eyeball".

Just to be absolutely complete, there needs to be a Global Variable called "WhenToStopDay" and "WhenToStopHour" no quotes but exactly as I have typed in the Global Variables and set at something like "5" and "20". Sorry for being pedantic nut I find that precise instructions are the best, well at least nearly precise just in case I have made a mistake. This is not difficult to do. Open Tools GoTo Global Variables click add and you are there. Ignore all the others.

Edit: The old lines will be cleared when a new week starts on Wednesday.

I hope that all makes sense.

--- 帖子 #1337 ---
Some neat analysis right there, wish this forum was full of this, a lot more useful than what is usually posted. Your going to need at least 10 times more data to say anything statistically viable enough to trade on, but imo this is the way to go for sure. Also try to see if you recognise any patterns of where losses or bigger wins come from, by looking at hundreds of trades you often get to a second edge in the system.

Quick remark about your earlier statement though: risking 5% on a single position is absolute madness. Both from a risk standpoint (not even including black swan events) and from a profit standpoint, often such big risk factors decrease the potential profit instead of increasing potential profits, i'd suggest doing the maths on this a few times as a good indicator of what to expect. Besides even in a winning system this would lead to periods of at least 80% drawdown, some people can handle this, 99.9% cannot.

Otherwise your on the right track man, stay on it!

--- 帖子 #1352 ---
Yes 5% on 1 pair is a lot, but especially on 1 trade, no matter how good the odds are. Seeing as your results will be (mostly) randomised if you do this for a while it's quite easy to hit a few losers in a row. Also it's very much possible to lose more then your sl on any position, so if this is 5 and there is a sudden move your whole account can easily be blown, if not more then what you deposited.

But why would you want to risk such high amounts anyway, just find the pairs that work best (3-4 is more than enough) and trade those, some diversity at least (in pairs but not really diversified in market conditions seeing as you trade them at the same time). Apart from that it would be completely insane to gain 5% per week and expect this to be consistent. If you would even make 0.5% every week you would be a millionaire in a few years only. Focus on where to find the highest % trades, not on increasing risk unnecessarily.

All the best

--- 帖子 #1361 ---
No problem in arguing, it's quarantine time so for this once we all have enough time anyway hehe.

But I understand the logic, ofcourse a really small account it doesn't matter. But then again the real trading (the fulltimejob type) is not really done on small accounts no matter what people might argue against this.

all that aside, in extreme news events the size does definitely matter. Your loss is still smaller in that situation, because you traded less volume. Losing 5% of equity 10 times over makes a 50% loss, losing 0.5% of equity 10 times over makes a 5% loss only. But perhaps most importantly losing a 5% position 100 times over makes a 500% loss and this can (and on many occasions has )definitely happen(ed) to people

--- 帖子 #1374 ---
Thats the good stuff right there, nice work!

Anything you noticed while looking at all those trades? any patterns, certain circumstances that made the trades better? That's usually where the juice is

If the edge is good enough as is you can trade it like this, just doing the best pairs might be enough for a prolonged edge. But usually when looking at a lot of trades you start to notice 'stuff' that makes certain trades a lot better over others, and then you can either increase equity on those trades. Personally when I find the extra edge those are then the only trades I take, no reason to trade anything other than the best setups.

the added edge could be anything; patterns, market circumstances, metadata etc.

Good luck!

And remember that you'll need a whole lot more data in order to really make it (like hundreds times more, both # of trades and variables per trade)

--- 帖子 #1388 ---
Yes, you need to place the EA on each chart that you want to trade, and leave your PC on (or use a VPS).

The EA opens market orders, not pending orders, so you only get trades as and when they trigger.

The default trigger is when price touches the entry line, but you can drop the chart down to, say, M30 and set the "Enter on break and CLOSE" parameter to true, and it will then open a trade only when the price closes on or above the entry line.

--- 帖子 #1394 ---
ah very nice, exactly the kind of patterns I was talking about, good stuff

And yeah, inputting all data in excel is timeconsuming, but then you can do a lot more stuff with the data once you find new angles. Ofcourse the 'easiest' way to do this is to import tick or 1m data and let excel do all the analysis, but setting this up for a new strategy is still quite time consuming even with good excell skills, and this way you don't have the advantage of gaining new insights just from seeing hundreds of trades.

For example normally when I research a breakout strategy I at least include Date (full date), Time, bars until trade trigger, sl size, directional move in pips, with monthly direction or not, with weekly direction or not and anything else you might want to research. Take into account that unless you highly suspect it might be usefull that it's not worth including as this does cost a lot of time. Especially because you need at the very least 500 trades to say anything statistically relevant at all, while in reality you want at least 2000 trades. This last part is where automating everything obviously comes in.

--- 帖子 #1404 ---
Ok, here is the code to produce the analysis .csv file which will be put in the Files folder under MQL. It has to go there no choice.

I haven't done anything to make it user friendly for configuration but a bit of thought you can see how it works.

The important bit is:

init section change Analyse to 1 if you want details for that pair

The number of Days analysed is set in the input section.

I have built this as an EA and not a script as I was getting some strange results as a script and thought it easier to test/fix.

Add it as an EA to a blank chart. It only runs when it is added or something changes like changing the timeframe.

It doesn't do anything else.

A sample for GBPJPY attatched

I'm am still checking results but if anyone does look at it and there are errors or additions let me know.

--- 帖子 #1405 ---
Again, good stuff!

Most of the variables are easy to understand indeed, and as long as you have succes per trade (so R:R reached), you can always test it for different variables and that's all that really matters.

% profit should just be the R:R reached imo. I usually just take the breakout range in pips, and the maximum move in pips, add in the spread (which i input as a variable) and divide those

so breakout range is 50 pips, maximum move is 200 pips, R:R is 1:4.

Seeing as you have 2 options for close here, friday close or a set R:R with a friday close if that isn't reached, recording the seperate maximum move that is reached during the week should be enough I think, unless i'm missing something.

--- 帖子 #1406 ---
Also vis a vis more variables, it would be interesting to know wether the trade was in accordance with the monthly/yearly direction. Monthly is most likely a lot more interesting than yearly. Can be calculated by measuring the distance between the trade open and the monthly open. Positive number in pips would be in accordance with monthly direction (and by measuring in pips you would see how strong the move is) and negative number would indicate against the monthly direction.

A lot of systems perform better when traded with monthly or weekly direction (yearly for longer term trades), some perform a lot better in strong moves (so far from open) and some perform better from consolidation type situations (so close to open)

--- 帖子 #1411 ---
Yes optimal R:R calculations are endless and partly pointless, optimization will just lead to futile results, as is the case with nearly all optimization on past results.

It's mainly just to get an indication; is it better to trade for long term gains, or are the breakouts usually short and then reverse. I mean who is to say an R:R of 1:.5 might not yield infinitely better results (just as an example). For example the main strategy I trade I use 1:10 TP's only, while it is theoretically also possible to be profitable on 1:1 and 1:2 etc the higher tp's are statistically a lot better, but eventually the number 10 is just practical, 11.2 would be optimal, but again over-optimization is just always lurking around the corner.

Perhaps I completely miss you point here though, because I don't fully understand what part of this way of viewing R:R you say you can't wrap your head around.

also MA can be good, does roughly the same thing. Monthly open is my personal preference as it's more objective than an MA number

--- 帖子 #1413 ---
I actually think we are on the same page. I have put in the MA direction based on a two 21MAs over a 5 day period. Sufficient to get a general direction.

MA1=iMA(name,1440,55,0,MODE_SMA,PRICE_CLOSE,cnt);

MA2=iMA(name,1440,55,0,MODE_SMA,PRICE_CLOSE,cnt+5);

if(MA1>MA2) {Trend="Long";}

if(MA1<MA2) {Trend="Short";

--- 帖子 #1443 ---
OK, so here is my opinion on this strategy.

I think the main reason why this is working, is because current market conditions are making it work. Take away the conditions that are fueling this strategy, and it will likely cease to perform as well as it has been thus far.

In other words, this strategy is more like gambling in my opinion. It works for now, but there may be no longevity to it. It's important to understand this.

Nothing beats Technical Analysis. I would hope the people using this strategy agree with this, because if a time comes when it no longer works, and you have been lazy and haven't learned how to do technical analysis, not only will your cash cow run out of milk, but you will be desperately scrambling to find the next best thing and likely lose time and money in the process.

The point I am making here is don't put all your eggs in one basket. Learn how to do proper technical analysis. It will be far more beneficial to you in the long run than this strategy likely ever will be.

I'm not saying you should quit the strategy. Use it for as long as it works, but be sure to delve deeper into understanding how the markets work and how to read price action. You will be thankful you did.

Range trading can generally be implemented at any time, but it proves to be most effective when the forex market lacks direction, with no discernible long-term trend in sight. On the other hand, range trading proves to be at its weakest during a trending market, especially if market directional bias isn’t accounted for.

--- 帖子 #1491 ---
Thanks for the feedback.

Having looked at the charts, I suspect that it's to do with price moving after the order has been triggered.

The EA won't place an order exactly on the entry line - the entry line is there purely as a visual marker for the trader - rather it is waiting for the price to reach OR EXCEED the trigger price.  It then calculates the entry price based on the CURRENT PRICE at that time.

So, if the price is moving quickly, it is possible for the price to be a few pips higher (or even lower) than the trigger point.

--- 帖子 #1493 ---

--- 帖子 #1494 ---
Sure, no problem.

Most trailing stops have two parts to them:The number of pips to trail by (the trail distance). The number of pips to move the stop by (the trail step). E.g. if you set the trail distance to 20 and the trail step to 5, the stop will stay where it is until the price is more than 25 pips ahead of the stop, and the stop will then be moved up by 5 pips.

This method is usually used to provide the price with some breathing room, but to then lock in some additional profit each time the price makes a higher high.

If you set the trail step to zero, this removes the 'stepping' feature.

E.g. if you set the trail distance to 20, and the step to 0, the stop will stay where it is until the price is more than 20 pips ahead of the stop, and the stop will then be moved to 20 pips behind the current price.

I hope that all makes, sense, but please ask if you have any further questions.

--- 帖子 #1499 ---
Also called slippage. Any market order on Mt4 should define an amount of slippage when the ea sends the order. This is one of the differences between using stop orders as they are executed when hit. There are of course pros and cons as I detailed some time ago. Pending orders are not conditional whereas market ones can be. Pending orders are sitting on the brokers server so once set you can shut down and wait for Friday.  Market orders require your PC to be on all the time. No right or wrong just different trade offs.  Of course there are 100s of ways to program this. Trust that helps.

Good trading

--- 帖子 #1500 ---
Thanks, but not quite: slippage is where the price moves from the price that the order is requesting, and if the new price is sufficiently far from the requested price, then the order will be rejected. My EA has a setting for it which I've defaulted to 2 pips, to avoid orders being rejected when slippage is small, and records errors due to slippage and shows them on the information panel.

But this isn't slippage that we were talking about, rather I was trying to explain the fact that the EA won't necessarily open the order exactly on the signal line (like a pending would most likely do), because the price can go higher before the EA detects that it now needs to place an order. In the example given, the order was opened 5.5 pips higher than the signal line. If it had been due to slippage then the order would have been rejected and an error recorded in the logs and shown on screen, so it was more likely a small spike in price beyond the signal line.

--- 帖子 #1521 ---
Damn, sorry I didn't keep better notes when I did all that viusal backtesting. oh well, maybe someone else will out do me and come up with much better and in depth stats. Just to remind everyone, we're not looking for "averages". We are looking at "frequency distribution" (a mathematical function showing the number of instances in which a variable takes each of its possible values.) For example it would be nice to know how many TP's and SL's a pair hit when the range was between 20-30, 30-40, 40-50, etc...We wouldn't be looking for the average range and the average amount of times it hit 1:1, 2:1, 3:1.

--- 帖子 #1569 ---
MoTuBo_EA Version 1.02

Having used the EA for all of my trades this past week, and based on feedback from others, I have made some small amendments to my EA, and recommend that anyone using previous versions upgrade to this version.

Changes:Removed the option of entering a trade on the break and CLOSE of a candle above the signal line. It turned out that this actually caused 3 losses which would have been wins! When adding the EA to a chart after Tuesday, it would immediately open a trade if the price was beyond the signal line. This has been fixed. Added a trigger factor for the Moving Average Trailing Stop. This is a multiplier of the stop loss. e.g. if the factor is set to 1, when the price reaches a profit of 1 x the stop loss, the trailing stop is triggered and the stop then follows the EMA line, using the period specified. For the Moving Average trailing stop, the M30 timeframe is recommended (and you will need to set the TP Calc Method to "None").

As always, any feedback is gratefully received.

--- 帖子 #1581 ---
You have to think of the SLs and TPs from the start of the range, not the start of the entry. So yes, 55% will result in a tighter SL than 45% since it is nearer to the entry, but further away from start of range.

--- 帖子 #1592 ---
Ah, thanks, that is a bug (which I have now fixed) and will be ok in the next version.

For now, simply set the "lock in pips" value to something othr than zero and it should work OK.

Break even and trailing stop ae two different things. but they can be used together.

Break even, is where you move the stop to your entry point (thus breaking even) when the price is a certain amount in profit (either in fixed pip value or a factor of the initial stop loss).  You can slo tell it to lock in profit by specifying how many pips profit to move the stop loss to.

Trailing stop does exactly what it say: the stop loss is moved periodically to follow the price each time the price moves a certain amount ahead.  There are numerous ways of moving the stop, and my EA provides a few of them.  There's no right or wrong setting really, it's simply up to you as to how you want your trades to be managed.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1664 ---
Hi, The timer is used to refresh the information panel (to avoid using too many resources on your PC), so if that hasn't been set for some reason, then the information panel won't be being updated.

The information panel is for information only (I have it turned off on my VPS), and the EA should be doing all of its monitoring in real time, regardless of what the panel says.

I am not aware of any reason as to why the timer cannot be set. Could you show me a screenshot of the error in the log please? I'm looking specifically for the error number - I ought to be able to work out the reason from that.

Thanks.

EDIT: I've just found out that setting timers can sometimes fail on slower PCs, or PCs using up a lot of resources (e.g. running lots of EAs).  I've made a small change that repeatedly attempt to set the time until it eventually succeeds.  There will be errors in the log, but the EA should eventually set the timer.

--- 帖子 #1686 ---
Hi Transmat,

I had coded this in an old version of an EA for other system, I don't remember full testing it though but you may if you want to.
Inserted Code double CalculateStakeByEquity(int stakePercent ) {
double oneLotMargin = MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_MARGINREQUIRED);
double lotMM = (AccountEquity() / 3) / oneLotMargin * stakePercent / 100;
double lotStep = MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_LOTSTEP);
return NormalizeDouble(lotMM / lotStep, 0) * lotStep;
}

Note: I don't know why it's dividing by 3 there, it might be related to the system

--- 帖子 #1705 ---
But then I guess you will only be trading a handful of pairs using this system then, because you'd effectively be managing 3x per pair. (which is a lot of work for me)

This actually got me thinking. One of the reasons I like this system is that there is a sort of built in diversification.
1st you have long and short pairs ready in case the market goes either way, 2nd you can trade a number of pairs and don't really have to worry about currency correlation (At least I don't, since I trade all 28 in both direction). 3rd, you have a high probability of good solid movement in one direction during Wed, Thur, and Fri. I think it was Erebus that pointed out that you can trade just about anything that moves with this system.

What I mean is, I look at it from a probability perspective across a "bucket" of trades, rather than relying on just a few good ones. Meaning of all these 20+ "strong" pairs I currently have opened, I am betting on the probability that at least 40% will hit TP. So for 20 pairs, 40% win-rate, assuming 2:1 Reward-to-Risk Ratio and $10 Risk. This is how it would look like:

WIN 20 * 40% * $10 * 2 = $160
LOSE 20 * 60% * $10 * 1 = $120

I would still be up by $40 even if 60% of my trades hit SL.
Not the most lucrative win, but If this holds true overtime, this can compound.

--- 帖子 #1711 ---
What killed your profit was money management: i.e. you used the same position sizing for all pairs regardless of the stop size.

e.g. EURAUD had a stop loss of 431 pips (probably would have been better to skip that one), and assuming your account is around €250, that means that at a lot size of 0.04, you're risking 38% of your account, on just the one trade!

Whereas on USDCAD, the stop loss was only 145 pips, so the lot size of 0.04 equates to roughly 15% of your account...still big, but better than the EURAUD trade.

So, USDCAD hit TP resulting in €36.94 profit, whereas EURAUD hit SL, resulting in a massive €103.77 loss...a net result of -€67. If you'd set EURAUD to 0.01 to match the pip sizing for USDCAD, your net result would have been around zero across those two pairs.

If you had used the money management feature and set a risk size of 10% and the "Trade if less than minimum" to "false", the EA would have skipped the EURAUD trade, but entered the USDCAD trade at 0.02 pips, which would have resulted in roughly a €25 profit instead of a €67 loss.

The lesson being: money management is key. It's no good setting fixed lot sizes and then hoping for the best...you WILL lose over time.

If you're not going to use the money management feature in the EA, then you really ought to decide on a maximum amount you are willing to risk on each trade, and then calculate the appropriate position sizing yourself on Tuesday evening/Wednesday morning, and enter the fixed lot sizes into each EA. I recommend using the position sizing calculator at myfxbook: https://www.myfxbook.com/forex-calcu.../position-size

That said, it's difficult to do this on such a small account size - you really need to have a minimum of around $1000 in order to make good use of money management.

--- 帖子 #1714 ---
I am using the defaults, which is 1% of account balance per trade.  But for that, you need a larger account size - over $1000 preferably.

If you have a smaller account size, and are willing to take the risk, then simply increase the risk% based on your account size vs $1000 - e.g. for $250, use 4%, for $500 use 2%, etc.

You will miss out on some trades due to the stop loss being too large, but then that may not be a bad thing...
