--- 帖子 #1745 ---
MoTuBo_EA Version 1.041

Changes:Fixed divide by zero error in Break Even routine. Fixed the "UseMinimumLots=false" function (it was being ignored and always used minimum lots). Corrected the calculation for the end of the Monday-Tuesday range period. Amended the entry trigger to use Bid price for long entries (this should reduce entries triggering due to widening spreads). Fixed the MA Trailing Stop from triggering simply when the Stop Loss was in profit (meaning you can now use Break Even and MA Trailing Stop together). Corrected the TP details displayed in the information panel. Information panel is now left displayed at the end of a testing session. A number of small efficiency improvements. NB: you should use this version in preference to all previous versions.

NBB: there have been no changes in settings - all defaults are as they were.

I've been getting quite a few PMs asking how to do things, and what various settings mean, so I thought I'd answer most of them here.

Money Management

This governs how lot sizes for trades are calculated, and there are three methods:
Attached Image

You select which method you want to use and then set the associated setting(s) (Fixed lots, Lots per 100 of balance or Risk percentage.

For Risk Percentage, you can choose what value to use as the basis of the percentage calculation:
Attached Image

Lots Size Maximum and Minimum
Attached Image

If you set a maximum lot size, and the calculation comes to more, the lot size will be capped at the value you set.

If you set a minimum lot size, and the calculation comes to less, the lot size will be increased to the value you set.

HOWEVER: if "Trade if less than minimum?" is set to false, and the cacluated lot size is lower than the minimum set, the EA will NOT enter the trade, as it is deemed too risky.

Break Even
Attached Image

There are three settings:No break even: basically, don't use the break even. Pips profit: moves stop to break even (i.e. the entry price) when the price is in profit by the specified number of pips. Factor of Stop Loss: moves the stop to break even when the price is in profit by a factor of the Stop Loss. e.g. If the stop loss is 150 pips and the factor is set to 0.5, when the price gets to 75 pips in proft (150 x 0.5), the stop loss will be moved to break even. Break Even Pips is the number of pips to use for method 1.

Pips to lock in on break even: when moving the stop to break even, you can specify a number of pips of profit to lock in.

Trailing Stop
Attached Image

There are four settings:No trailing stop. Regular trailing stop: triggered when the price is in profit by the Regular trailing stop start, and is moved in steps set in the Regular trailing stop step setting. Follow MA: the trailing stop is triggered when the price is in profit by the factor of the stop loss specified (e.g. if the stop loss is 150 pips and the factor is set to 0.75, the trailing stop is triggered when the price reaches 112 pips (150 x 0.75). The stop is then trailed along the line of a moving average with the period specified. Previous high/low: the trailing stop is moved when the previous three candles form a new low or high.

As ever, let me know if you find anything untoward.

--- 帖子 #1753 ---
Thanks.

The previous version was using Ask for length entries and Bid for short entries.  I have switched them fir this version.

For long, I use the Bid price so that widening spreads (usually the Ask price( doesn't trigger an entry too early.

For short, I use the Ask price for the same reason.

These only affect the entry. Once a trade is open, normal rules apply regarding the hitting of the stop loss.

--- 帖子 #1754 ---
Ok, I understand your reasons. For longs you are correct, but short trades will not trigger earlier when spreads are widening (actually they would trigger later if using the ask price). For shorts the bid price will not change. The only things can happen are:

1. "Normal Entry" short trade by bid price --> the ask price will be closer to the SL than without spread widening, but that's no problem

2. "Your EA version" short trade by ask price --> entry is much lower as it normally would (because ask price is at entry level and bid price way below)

So I would suggest to use the bid price for short entries and bid price for longs, too.

--- 帖子 #1772 ---
MoTuBO_EA Version 1.05

Changes:Added a time filter - trades will only open between these times. The information panel is now displayed immediately on startup. Corrected the routine that calculates the number of trades opened this week. Added a background to the information panel to make things clearer. Added options to display guide lines or not. Added options to display the weekly entry range box, or not. Amended guide lines to show price levels. Most of the new stuff is cosmetic, and allows you to dispense with using the MoTuBo_Indi (if you use it, that is).

The main feature is the addition of a time filter:
Attached Image

You can now specify the window in which trades will be opened, by specifying the from day and hour (defaults to Wednesday, 00:00) and the to day and hour (defaults to Friday, 22:00).

Here's the full screenshot with all info panels displayed:
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Happy trading!

--- 帖子 #1785 ---
Attached Image

Try this if you're using Windows 10. I use a 4K display and it worked for me.

Right click on your MT4's .exe file or the shortcut on your desktop. Next, right click on Properties then the Compatibility tab. Click on Change high DPI settings then at the lower part of the box you'll see High DPI scaling override. Check the box beside Override high DPI scaling behavior. and slide the pull down menu to System (enhanced). Click OK and OK to get out.

The strategy is so simple that, if you're happy using the spreadsheet and entering trades manually, then there's very little past the first couple of posts in this thread worth reading.

Erebus did an excellent job at pointing out how we can use the Fibonacci tool in place of the spreadsheet, but again, if you're happy with the spreadsheet, then that's probably a step too far for you as well.

There's no obsession with EAs (at least on my part), but seeing as the strategy is so simple, and the trading week is reduced to just Wednesday/Thursday/Friday (or less for some), then what else is there to say in this thread?  I'm a coder by trade, so for me this is a perfect excuse to build something FOR ME, to help ME (because I'm lazy), but I offer it here for others to use if they want.  I suspect that the same goes for most of the others here who are coding their own EAs and scripts - it's all to make a tiresome task less tiresome while having some fun in the process.

But, I'm happy to join in with whatever other conversation you'd rather be having...

--- 帖子 #1799 ---
Yeah totally agree.

If it works why not use a bot? EA's can open multiple trades way more efficiently and error free than I usually can (ie. it won't miss setting that stoploss, or miss a crucial number, etc).

However from my experience, EA's WILL miss that one possible combination that it can't compensate for (ie. loss of internet for a second, broker manipulation, etc).

So I have a trust/mistrust relationship with bots. I use EA's to initiate the trade(s), double check the trades to confirm, then let them run their course without my greedy/fearful fingers hitting that close trade button, but keeping an eye on progress just in case.

MoTuBo_EA Version 1.06

First off: apologies to everyone who downloaded and installed 1.05 - I realise that this release is very soon after the previous version, however it is NOT an April Fools...there are one or two bugs which surfaced after release of 1.05 that for technical reasons didn't materialise in the Strategy Tester.

I was already making some minor tweaks, so have included these as part of this emergency bug fix version.

Changes:Fixed a divide by zero error in the trailing stop routine. Added an option to allow the range to be determined using the bodies of the candles instead of the wicks (the default is to use the wicks). Fixed guide length on start of new month! Increased the frequency with which the info panel is updated. A couple of minor efficiency improvement to reduce load on the terminal. New option for range determination:

--- 帖子 #1844 ---
Thanks.

Looking at the messages, you will see it says "Open orders: 9 (this symbol: 1)".

This means that you currently have 9 orders open for this magic number, and one of them is for the current symbol.

The EA ignores any orders with a different magic number. I suggest that you double-check the magic number against those 9 open orders.

To prove this, I've changed the magic number on the EA on one of my charts, and now get the following:
Attached Image

As you will see it says 'Open orders: 0 (this symbol: 0)' but I actually have 12 trades running right now.

I changed it back, and you will see it's updated again:
Attached Image

--- 帖子 #1861 ---
Sorry but I have to disagree. Not sure what you mean by daily market profile though. The high and lows are absolute values, whether true or not, they are what we see on our screens. The bodies ie Open/Close are only a snapshot for probably a few seconds when the day changes. When trading stocks where a market does open and close and traders go home and think there is real value in these numbers. In a continuous process like Forex they are purely transient. The open and close are imo irrelevant.

This is a breakout strategy and using open/close rather than hi/lo means you could more likely be trading into areas of resistance/support rather than breaking into new ground. Not 100% certain but just reducing probability.

Just my way of looking at it. I have been wrong before.

--- 帖子 #1864 ---
Any major open like NY or London could be considered start of the day. Imo London open is probably the most followed open time.

Candle wicks in market profile terms represent excess in the price discovery. The body of the candle is where most trades are executed. In general about 70% of all trades fall in the value area - core of the value area is balance - price will break out of balance and eventually out of value area to search for a new balance (most accepted price).

Does that make a diff for the MoTu system? I don't know - Mentioned this before known energy trader at Intl FC Stone uses the Mon/Tue value area to allocate his trades.

.

I mentioned the 55% SL before. If the range between Monday and Tuesday happen to make the swing high and swing low and we throw a fib on it, of course there is a chance that price returns to the 50 fib, which in our case is our SL. So why not just extend our SL just a little bit to either 55% or even 60% if you want to play it a little more safe. You can either also extend your TP a little bit to maintain your 1:1 ratio, or just take it as is and settle for a little bit less than 1:1.

--- 帖子 #1884 ---
Hi, and thank you for supplying screen shots - they were most helpful!

Yes, as the error message says, it didn't open the order because the lot size was too small. You are using money management (i.e. the EA will automatically calculate the lot size for the order based on your account balance) and have selected to risk 1% of your account balance per trade. The EA has calculated the lot size based on this and the size of the stop loss, and determined that the lot size is probably less than 0.01 lots. You have set a minimum lot size of 0.01 lots, so the EA will attempt to use this value. You have also set the option "Trade if less than minimum" to false, so this stops the EA from entering the trade, because the risk is too great. You have a couple of ways around this:Change the "Trade is less than minimum" to true: how ever you could end up risking more than you intended. Used fixed lots, and set the lot size yourself. Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1885 ---
Currently, no, but the coding is there to support it, so it could be enabled.

The issue with doing this though is the rules that need to be put into place...Do you allow a second trade while the first is still open? Do you allow a second trade if the first lost? Do you allow a second trade if the first won? If you allow a second trade, do you want to limit it to the same direction or the opposite direction of the first, or no limits at all? How about a third, or fourth trade?... Basically, it gets to being a bit of a minefield rather quickly, and is more likely to be easier to open new trades manually, on those few occasions that you want to use this feature.

If there's a demand for it, and I can get a good idea of how it should work (without being too complicated!) then I may build it in.

Back test results don't mean anything at all. The only thing a back test is good for is to test the functionality of an EA or Indicator. Results are meaningless. The only way to know if something is profitable or not is to forward test and keep notes/stats. Forex is a marathon. No way around it. The sooner you accept that the better off you will be.

where you see a negative pair and the candle, are both the same colour.
This is where an entry point will occur,
you just need to determine which way to

--- 帖子 #2135 ---
Hi FX5Star,

A different MagicNumber is required for each pair otherwise there may be interference and if an order is executed or the entry level is already exceeded on a pair it will not pass the others in the same direction if this MagicNumber is identical.

Here's how I put it into action:

First of all, after placing the EA on the graph, I also place the indicator "TuBo_One Day_Indicator_corrected_V_1.1" with the same parameters as the EA, this in order to visualize if the levels are correct when the orders in waiting will be passed.

I deactivate Autotrading (at the top of the left side of the mt4 platform)

I open the table to adjust all the parameters and I check if the "authorize live trading" box is checked and I close it.

I reactivate Autotrading and I reopen the table of parameters and I click on "OK". BuyStop and SellStop orders are placed and we can immediately see if they are on the right levels as well as the StopLoss.

To place orders on another pair, I deactivate Autotrading again and open a new chart on a new pair and open the EA table again to change the MagicNumber and the position size if it must be different and other parameters if necessary.

I close the table, I reactivate Autotrading, I reopen the table and click again on "OK".

And so on for the other pairs. (don't forget to change the MagicNumber for each pair).

This procedure is somewhat similar to that of a script and you can turn off the PC once all the orders have been placed and simply monitor from time to time and intervene manually to adjust the strategy if necessary.

And if you leave the PC on, it will manage position tracking.

Keep me posted to let me know if your problem is resolved.

--- 帖子 #2138 ---
Hi! First of all thanks for keeping the code of the EA open. That's how it should be in this community. Thumbs up!

I am thinking of adding another parameter: open/close time that forms the virtual breakout box. Meaning, not simply using hi/lo from Monday-Tuesday but being able to say:

box should start at e.g. Monday 8:00 GMT and stop at Tuesday 17:00 GMT (do the hours sound familiar ;-) ?)

The reason is simple: I put endless numbers of fibo lines over the boxes and found out, that the support and resistance are formed from LO Monday until LC Tuesday. Okay, we do not know the direction, but IF a pair is leaving the box, then it normally uses these fibo lines to form the candles high/low.

I am just analyzing the code of the above EA to find an elegant way to determine the hi/lo without wasting precious processor time.

Something like this, taken from the Mo_TuBo Indicator:
Inserted Code   //determine hi/lo
boxStartShift = iBarShift(NULL,0,tBoxStart);
boxEndShift   = iBarShift(NULL,0,tBoxEnd);
boxHigh = High[iHighest(NULL,0,MODE_HIGH,(boxStartShift-boxEndShift+1),boxEndShift)];
boxLow  = Low[iLowest(NULL,0,MODE_LOW,(boxStartShift-boxEndShift+1),boxEndShift)];

The main thing that I have realized, and the concept you should take from this, use it as an analysis method and not purely a trading system.

Sure, you will still get great entries and then price reverses back 100% the other way - it's not you and it's not the method - the markets does what it wants.

Definitively incorporate the analysis part into whatever you use now; me, I use the longer term trend.

There are only two types of trades. Continuation or Reversal. Trend or Fade. Call it whatever you want, but whenever anyone places a trade they are always implicitly making a bet that prices will extend in the prior direction or will reverse.

To me, this method is obviously best for entering a continuation or trend, and that suits me as a breakout trader.

Probably said too much but hey, I'm just like anyone else, struggling to get ahead, figure out what will make a dollar from week to week.

--- 帖子 #2244 ---
For the Metatrader 4 users, there is a way to plot 2 lines for the Mon Tue range, 1 line for the exact high and low, and the other for a buffer zone of your choice.

The buffer zone is just an area that you can choose to use as you wish; does it show extra confirmation by a close below (or above)? is it just an area where you can take a trade because you know entries don't have to be that precise?

This is achieved by using 2 instances of Daily Line Boxes(1), the buffer zone can only be in pips, not percentage, so unfortunately when you use a Template, all pairs will have the same zone, be it 10 pips or 15 pips according to your settings.

Here are the settings I used, you can change to suit your charts, the main thing is to change the very last line "UniqueID" as shown, so it knows it a second application.

And of course, the colors, the clearance pips, any problem please ask. With the second instance, you can see that I have it to display on the D1 or Daily chart. This make it very easy to check every chart on Wednesday, on Daily, to spot any potential setups.

As usual, any feedback, comments, likes, criticisms and suggestions are welcomed

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2260 ---
I have no idea what you mean by "exhaustive data" but I will explain what transpires...

Buy and sell stop orders are placed at "entry" levels. When either is triggered, the other stop order is cancelled.

When (or if) price reaches "secure profit" level, I raise stop to breakeven plus a few pips in profit (usually 10 pips profit).

When (or if) price nears the "TP" level, I raise stop to "secure profit" level.

When (or if) price goes negative, my stop loss is in place at 50% fib level... and there have been stop outs.

That's it to the strategy. No "exhaustive data" to show except for the results over the past 3 weeks.

This is a simple strategy. Don't over complicate it.

I won't be "bragging" about my results... I'll just be a spectator in this thread.

Good luck

Markets (PRICE) can do 3 things, according to Stacey Burke

1 - Breakout - Pullback - Continue

2 - Breakout - Pullback - Range

3 - Breakout - Pullback - Reverse

An example of #1, both as last week's price action, and a larger scale move of the same Breakout - Pullback - Continue

And the guy wonders why the EA didn't work last week

So entry could be either Monday or Tuesday, Wednesday is payday!

--- 帖子 #2337 ---
My favorite candle formation is on a HTF (D,W,M......the higher the better) when in a UPTREND price sets a new swing high with a RED candle or if in a DOWNTREND price sets a new swing low with a GREEN candle. I trade the reversal of the trend on the start of the following candle......BUT, THERE MUST BE LOTS OF ROOM TO THE LEFT. By the looks of this chart you post, it's very close to being a really good signal imo. Definitely worth placing a trade on imo.

EDIT: Just take a look at the High to the left. It was set by a Red candle it looks like. Then look at the big move down afterwards. I could care less that it's a pinbar. That was just an added bonus.

EDIT 2: I just noticed that the move UP just prior was also started with a White candle at the end of the downtrend.

--- 帖子 #2341 ---
Hello Erebus

Thank you for posting this chart, this is exactly what I meant in my previous posts, weekly trend is up, last week is a down bar.

Now we want to establish a bias for the coming week, which one do we go by? The trend or last bar? At the open of the week we want to set a limit order 30-40 pips above or below the line as HE says, if we go with the trend we should set it below the line if we go with last bar's direction we should set it above the line. Or if we want to observe price action on M-T, if bias is long we should pay attention to the lows on those days and vice versa.

I am trying to make this method work in my favour as much as possible because I like it, I am not criticizing it.

Myself I would choose direction of the last bar as the bias and make it a rule.

I think and I certainly hope that everyone knows about the theory to sell (or buy) at a retracement level of an engulfing candle.

Usually, that means around 50% which is not a Fibonacci number, more of a Gann number I believe.

Anyway, let's check that out on the daily chart, remember where the ideal place to sell (or buy) is? Yes, the WICK of the Weekly candle.

--- 帖子 #2399 ---
Bit of an update for the week of April 26 - 30, 2021

A couple of things I used for this backtest, introduce a Wednesday time window, which means if the trade is not triggered on Wednesday, no trade for the week.

The 2nd thing would be using a Stop Loss of 0.5 of ADR (20) and a Take Profit of 1 x ADR (20), moving to Break Even when 1 to 1 level is reached.

Pretty standard risk management that all should be familiar with. A move of 1 x ADR (20) is not asking that much when there are 2.5 days left in the week.

And as I used Metatrader 5, I was able to use my PriceBox indicator which has the ability to set a variable Buffer size as per the original rules.

I used 10% of the Mon Tue range; this allows for the different volatility of each pair.

I used the guideline of waiting for a close on the 1-hour candle beyond the Mon Tue range and setting the pending order at the Buffer price level.

The final gain on the week shows 9 R, so if the risk per trade was 1% that means a gain of 9%, just don't expect me to ever report a profit in pips.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2400 ---
Here is an example of how simple this trade can be. For me, EURCAD is a notoriously difficult pair to get any pips, and yet this looks easy.

ADR (20) is 97 so, round to 100, make the Stop Loss 50 pips, the Take Profit 100 pips.

Did anyone notice on the report that there are 8 full TP trades and 8 full SL trades?

This is the stock standard teachings of FX trading, use a Risk-Reward of 2 to 1, and even with 50% losers you still make money.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2415 ---
No, the idea is to find the RANGE using the highest price of Monday or Tuesday and the lowest price of Monday or Tuesday.

The absolute HIGH and the absolute LOW will be the SAME on every time frame.

Then you can make a plan to enter at that price or at some percentage of the range above or below that price, or at a certain number of pips above or below that range.

So, it is impossible to say which candle will cross the chosen price line, it could be on Wednesday, it could be on Thursday.

It might even be on Friday if that is your plan. And I promise you, when it crosses the line, the time frame doesn't matter.

--- 帖子 #2445 ---
It can return phenomenal results on the right week, absolutely...

But it will eat your account on other weeks...

That's why I just recommend using it as an ANALYSIS method...

When you see a setup happening, other price action, strong & weak, fundamental situation and the stars lined up together...

Then you hit that pair(s) as hard as you can; it won't even happen every week, but when it does, usually on correlated pairs.

Also, it can help make the decision to stay out of the market, which can save you some time, money, and regrets.

The market can only move in 3 directions, just know where it is from week to week...

Good luck

Was attempting to show the fib settings I've found useful.

Entry level @ 14% either side of MonTue range.

--- 帖子 #2448 ---
++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

This hard stuff. After THOROUGHLY reviewing previous testing, the numbers are still positive, But not by much. Pairs I've tested, going back 40 weeks each, are; GU, GA, & Gchf.

• I eliminated large ranges. On GA, ranges over 180, GU & GChf ranges over 125. On all pairs, trades were closed prior to end of week. Most of those, were in a basic break even range.

• I did change Stop Loss levels to 30%, from 33%, as I noticed that when price reverses a normal amount, it rarely reaches 30%. If price goes beyond 30%, it's usually by quite a lot. It doesn't appear that using a larger SL, makes much sense.

• Another change is trailing the SL (once only). If price makes it half way to TP, my testing moves SL from 44 to 28(14% inside range). 44 being the distance from entry, at 14% beyond MT range, back to 30% inside range.

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
